 229: #if !MIN_VERSION_base(4,10,0)
 230: -- |Advances the given address by the given offset in bytes.
 231: --
 232: -- The new 'ForeignPtr' shares the finalizer of the original,
 233: -- equivalent from a finalization standpoint to just creating another
 234: -- reference to the original. That is, the finalizer will not be
 235: -- called before the new 'ForeignPtr' is unreachable, nor will it be
 236: -- called an additional time due to this call, and the finalizer will
 237: -- be called with the same address that it would have had this call
 238: -- not happened, *not* the new address.
 239: plusForeignPtr :: ForeignPtr a -> Int -> ForeignPtr b
 240: plusForeignPtr (ForeignPtr addr guts) (I# offset) = ForeignPtr (plusAddr# addr offset) guts
 241: {-# INLINE [0] plusForeignPtr #-}
 242: {-# RULES
"ByteString plusForeignPtr/0" forall fp .
   plusForeignPtr fp 0 = fp
 #-}
 246: #endif

 265: 
 266: -- | Most operations on a 'ByteString' need to read from the buffer
 267: -- given by its @ForeignPtr Word8@ field.  But since most operations
 268: -- on @ByteString@ are (nominally) pure, their implementations cannot
 269: -- see the IO state thread that was used to initialize the contents of
 270: -- that buffer.  This means that under some circumstances, these
 271: -- buffer-reads may be executed before the writes used to initialize
 272: -- the buffer are executed, with unpredictable results.
 273: --
 274: -- 'deferForeignPtrAvailability' exists to help solve this problem.
 275: -- At runtime, a call @'deferForeignPtrAvailability' x@ is equivalent
 276: -- to @pure $! x@, but the former is more opaque to the simplifier, so
 277: -- that reads from the pointer in its result cannot be executed until
 278: -- the @'deferForeignPtrAvailability' x@ call is complete.
 279: --
 280: -- The opaque bits evaporate during CorePrep, so using
 281: -- 'deferForeignPtrAvailability' incurs no direct overhead.
 282: --
 283: -- @since 0.11.5.0
 284: deferForeignPtrAvailability :: ForeignPtr a -> IO (ForeignPtr a)
 285: forall a .
lq_tmp$x##4319:(GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtr a) -> (GHC.Types.IO (GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtr a))deferForeignPtrAvailability (ForeignPtr addr0# guts) = IO $ \{VV##4346 : (GHC.Prim.State# {VV##4344 : GHC.Prim.RealWorld | $k_##4345}) | $k_##4347}s0 ->

 297: unsafeDupablePerformIO :: IO a -> a
 298: -- Why does this exist? In base-4.15.1.0 until at least base-4.18.0.0,
 299: -- the version of unsafeDupablePerformIO in base prevents unboxing of
 300: -- its results with an opaque call to GHC.Exts.lazy, for reasons described
 301: -- in Note [unsafePerformIO and strictness] in GHC.IO.Unsafe. (See
 302: -- https://hackage.haskell.org/package/base-4.18.0.0/docs/src/GHC.IO.Unsafe.html#line-30 .)
 303: -- Even if we accept the (very questionable) premise that the sort of
 304: -- function described in that note should work, we expect no such

 306: -- unboxing!)

 313: -- | A space-efficient representation of a 'Word8' vector, supporting many
 314: -- efficient operations.
 315: --
 316: -- A 'ByteString' contains 8-bit bytes, or by using the operations from
 317: -- "Data.ByteString.Char8" it can be interpreted as containing 8-bit
 318: -- characters.
 319: --
 320: data ByteString = BS {-# UNPACK #-} !(ForeignPtr Word8) -- payload
 321:                      {-# UNPACK #-} !Int                -- length
 322:                      -- ^ @since 0.11.0.0
 323: 
 324: -- | Type synonym for the strict flavour of 'ByteString'.
 325: --
 326: -- @since 0.11.2.0
 327: type StrictByteString = ByteString
 328: 
 329: -- |
 330: -- @'PS' foreignPtr offset length@ represents a 'ByteString' with data
 331: -- backed by a given @foreignPtr@, starting at a given @offset@ in bytes
 332: -- and of a specified @length@.
 333: --
 334: -- This pattern is used to emulate the legacy 'ByteString' data
 335: -- constructor, so that pre-existing code generally doesn't need to
 336: -- change to benefit from the simplified 'BS' constructor and can
 337: -- continue to function unchanged.
 338: --
 339: -- /Note:/ Matching with this constructor will always be given a 0 offset,
 340: -- as the base will be manipulated by 'plusForeignPtr' instead.
 341: --
 342: pattern PS :: ForeignPtr Word8 -> Int -> Int -> ByteString
 343: pattern PS fp zero len <- {lq_tmp$x##5011 : GHC.Prim.Int# | lq_tmp$x##5011 == 0}BS fp ((0,) -> ({lq_tmp$x##5014 : GHC.Types.Int | lq_tmp$x##5014 == (lq_anf$##7205759403792830209##d9wt : int)}zero, len)) where

 466: 
 467: 
 468: -- | /O(n)/ Pack a null-terminated sequence of bytes, pointed to by an
 469: -- Addr\# (an arbitrary machine address assumed to point outside the
 470: -- garbage-collected heap) into a @ByteString@. A much faster way to
 471: -- create an 'Addr#' is with an unboxed string literal, than to pack a
 472: -- boxed string. A unboxed string literal is compiled to a static @char
 473: -- []@ by GHC. Establishing the length of the string requires a call to
 474: -- @strlen(3)@, so the 'Addr#' must point to a null-terminated buffer (as
 475: -- is the case with @\"string\"\#@ literals in GHC). Use 'Data.ByteString.Unsafe.unsafePackAddressLen'
 476: -- if you know the length of the string statically.
 477: --
 478: -- An example:
 479: --
 480: -- > literalFS = unsafePackAddress "literal"#
 481: --
 482: -- This function is /unsafe/. If you modify the buffer pointed to by the
 483: -- original 'Addr#' this modification will be reflected in the resulting
 484: -- @ByteString@, breaking referential transparency.
 485: --
 486: -- Note this also won't work if your 'Addr#' has embedded @\'\\0\'@ characters in
 487: -- the string, as @strlen@ will return too short a length.
 488: --
 489: unsafePackAddress :: Addr# -> IO ByteString
 490: lq_tmp$x##13567:GHC.Prim.Addr# -> (GHC.Types.IO Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString)unsafePackAddress GHC.Prim.Addr#addr# = do
 491: #if __GLASGOW_HASKELL__ >= 811
 492:     unsafePackLenAddress {VV##13577 : GHC.Types.Int | $k_##13578}(I# GHC.Prim.Int#(cstringLength# {lq_tmp$x##13573 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##13573 == addr###a85p}addr#)) {lq_tmp$x##13598 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##13598 == addr###a85p}addr#
 493: #else
 494:     l <- c_strlen (Ptr addr#)
 495:     unsafePackLenAddress (fromIntegral l) addr#
 496: #endif
 497: {-# INLINE unsafePackAddress #-}
 498: 
 499: -- | See 'unsafePackAddress'. This function is similar,
 500: -- but takes an additional length argument rather then computing
 501: -- it with @strlen@.
 502: -- Therefore embedding @\'\\0\'@ characters is possible.
 503: --
 504: -- @since 0.11.2.0
 505: unsafePackLenAddress :: Int -> Addr# -> IO ByteString
 506: lq_tmp$x##13519:GHC.Types.Int -> lq_tmp$x##13520:GHC.Prim.Addr# -> (GHC.Types.IO Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString)unsafePackLenAddress GHC.Types.Intlen GHC.Prim.Addr#addr# = do
 507: #if __GLASGOW_HASKELL__ >= 811
 508:     return Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString(BS (GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtr {lq_tmp$x##13533 : GHC.Word.Word8 | $k_##13532[VV##13531:=lq_tmp$x##13533][lq_tmp$x##13529:=addr###a85r][lq_tmp$x##13530:=GHC.ForeignPtr.FinalPtr]})(ForeignPtr {lq_tmp$x##13534 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##13534 == addr###a85r}addr# {lq_tmp$x##13535 : GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtrContents | lq_tmp$x##13535 == GHC.ForeignPtr.FinalPtr}FinalPtr) {lq_tmp$x##13547 : GHC.Types.Int | lq_tmp$x##13547 == len##a85q}len)

 510:     p <- newForeignPtr_ (Ptr addr#)

 512: #endif

 515: -- | See 'unsafePackAddress'. This function has similar behavior. Prefer
 516: -- this function when the address in known to be an @Addr#@ literal. In

 519: -- constructor for @ForeignPtrContents@.

 522: unsafePackLiteral :: Addr# -> ByteString

 532: 
 533: -- | See 'unsafePackLiteral'. This function is similar,
 534: -- but takes an additional length argument rather then computing
 535: -- it with @strlen@.
 536: -- Therefore embedding @\'\\0\'@ characters is possible.
 537: --

 539: unsafePackLenLiteral :: Int -> Addr# -> ByteString
 540: lq_tmp$x##5224:GHC.Types.Int -> lq_tmp$x##5225:GHC.Prim.Addr# -> Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteStringunsafePackLenLiteral GHC.Types.Intlen GHC.Prim.Addr#addr# =
 541: #if __GLASGOW_HASKELL__ >= 811
 542:   BS (GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtr {lq_tmp$x##5238 : GHC.Word.Word8 | $k_##5237[VV##5236:=lq_tmp$x##5238][lq_tmp$x##5234:=addr###a85u][lq_tmp$x##5235:=GHC.ForeignPtr.FinalPtr]})(ForeignPtr {lq_tmp$x##5239 : GHC.Prim.Addr# | lq_tmp$x##5239 == addr###a85u}addr# {lq_tmp$x##5240 : GHC.ForeignPtr.ForeignPtrContents | lq_tmp$x##5240 == GHC.ForeignPtr.FinalPtr}FinalPtr) {lq_tmp$x##5252 : GHC.Types.Int | lq_tmp$x##5252 == len##a85t}len

 569: 
 570: -- Unpacking bytestrings into lists efficiently is a tradeoff: on the one hand
 571: -- we would like to write a tight loop that just blasts the list into memory, on
 572: -- the other hand we want it to be unpacked lazily so we don't end up with a
 573: -- massive list data structure in memory.
 574: --
 575: -- Our strategy is to combine both: we will unpack lazily in reasonable sized
 576: -- chunks, where each chunk is unpacked strictly.
 577: --
 578: -- unpackBytes and unpackChars do the lazy loop, while unpackAppendBytes and
 579: -- unpackAppendChars do the chunks strictly.
 580: 
 581: unpackBytes :: ByteString -> [Word8]

      {lq_tmp$x##21687 : [a]<\lq_tmp$x##21688 VV -> {lq_tmp$x##21686 : a<p lq_tmp$x##21688> | true}> | len lq_tmp$x##21687 == 0} | VV == GHC.Types.[]}[]
 583:

 861:     -- The idea here is we first do a pass over the input list to determine:
 862:     --
 863:     --  1. is a copy necessary? e.g. @concat []@, @concat [mempty, "hello"]@,
 864:     --     and @concat ["hello", mempty, mempty]@ can all be handled without
 865:     --     copying.
 866:     --  2. if a copy is necessary, how large is the result going to be?
 867:     --
 868:     -- If a copy is necessary then we create a buffer of the appropriate size
 869:     -- and do another pass over the input list, copying the chunks into the
 870:     -- buffer. Also, since foreign calls aren't entirely free we skip over
 871:     -- empty chunks while copying.
 872:     --
 873:     -- We pass the original [ByteString] (bss0) through as an argument through
 874:     -- goLen0, goLen1, and goLen since we will need it again in goCopy. Passing
 875:     -- it as an explicit argument avoids capturing it in these functions'
 876:     -- closures which would result in unnecessary closure allocation.
 877:   where
 878:     -- It's still possible that the result is empty
 879:     lq_tmp$x##20590:{VV##20577 : [{VV##20572 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20573}]<\lq_tmp$x##20592 VV -> {VV##20575 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20576[lq_tmp$x##20574:=lq_tmp$x##20592][lq_tmp$x##20588:=lq_tmp$x##20592]}> | $k_##20578} -> lq_tmp$x##20591:{VV##20584 : [{VV##20579 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20580[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20590]}]<\lq_tmp$x##20593 VV -> {VV##20582 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20583[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20590][lq_tmp$x##20581:=lq_tmp$x##20593][lq_tmp$x##20589:=lq_tmp$x##20593]}> | $k_##20585[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20590]} -> {VV##20586 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | $k_##20587[ds_d9cM:=lq_tmp$x##20590][ds_d9cN:=lq_tmp$x##20591]}goLen0 _    []                     = {lq_tmp$x##20619 : Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.ByteString | lq_tmp$x##20619 == Data.ByteString.Internal.Type.empty}empty

 927: 
 928: {-
Note [Float error calls out of INLINABLE things]
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

If a function is marked INLINE or INLINABLE, then when ghc inlines or
specializes it, it duplicates the function body exactly as written.

This feature is useful for systems of rewrite rules, but sometimes
comes at a code-size cost.  One situation where this cost generally
comes with no compensating up-side is when the function in question
calls `error` or something similar.

Such an `error` call is not meaningfully improved by the extra context
inlining or specialization provides, and if inlining or specialization
happens in a different module from where the function was originally
defined, CSE will not be able to de-duplicate the error call floated
out of the inlined RHS and the error call floated out of the original
RHS.  See also https://gitlab.haskell.org/ghc/ghc/-/issues/23823

To mitigate this, we manually float the error calls out of INLINABLE
functions when it is possible to do so.
-}

1081: -- | This \"function\" has a superficial similarity to 'System.IO.Unsafe.unsafePerformIO' but
1082: -- it is in fact a malevolent agent of chaos. It unpicks the seams of reality
1083: -- (and the 'IO' monad) so that the normal rules no longer apply. It lulls you
1084: -- into thinking it is reasonable, but when you are not looking it stabs you
1085: -- in the back and aliases all of your mutable buffers. The carcass of many a
1086: -- seasoned Haskell programmer lie strewn at its feet.
1087: --
1088: -- Witness the trail of destruction:
1089: --
1090: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/bytestring/commit/71c4b438c675aa360c79d79acc9a491e7bbc26e7>
1091: --
1092: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/bytestring/commit/210c656390ae617d9ee3b8bcff5c88dd17cef8da>
1093: --
1094: -- * <https://github.com/haskell/aeson/commit/720b857e2e0acf2edc4f5512f2b217a89449a89d>
1095: --
1096: -- * <https://ghc.haskell.org/trac/ghc/ticket/3486>
1097: --
1098: -- * <https://ghc.haskell.org/trac/ghc/ticket/3487>
1099: --
1100: -- * <https://ghc.haskell.org/trac/ghc/ticket/7270>
1101: --
1102: -- * <https://gitlab.haskell.org/ghc/ghc/-/issues/22204>
1103: --
1104: -- Do not talk about \"safe\"! You do not know what is safe!
1105: --
1106: -- Yield not to its blasphemous call! Flee traveller! Flee or you will be
1107: -- corrupted and devoured!
1108: --

1226: -- We import bytestring_is_valid_utf8 both unsafe and safe. For small inputs
1227: -- we can use the unsafe version to get a bit more performance, but for large

1246: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1247: -- Haskell version of functions in fpstring.c
1248: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1249: 
1250: -- | Reverse n-bytes from the second pointer into the first
1251: c_reverse :: Ptr Word8 -> Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO ()
1252: c_reverse p1 p2 sz = Pure.reverseBytes p1 p2 (checkedCast sz)
1253: 
1254: -- | find maximum char in a packed string
1255: c_maximum :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO Word8
1256: c_maximum ptr sz = Pure.findMaximum ptr (checkedCast sz)
1257: 
1258: -- | find minimum char in a packed string
1259: c_minimum :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO Word8
1260: c_minimum ptr sz = Pure.findMinimum ptr (checkedCast sz)
1261: 
1262: -- | count the number of occurrences of a char in a string
1263: c_count :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> Word8 -> IO CSize
1264: c_count ptr sz c = checkedCast <$!> Pure.countOcc ptr (checkedCast sz) c
1265: 
1266: -- | count the number of occurrences of a char in a string
1267: c_count_ba :: ByteArray# -> Int -> Word8 -> IO CSize
1268: c_count_ba ba o c = checkedCast <$!> Pure.countOccBA ba o c
1269: 
1270: -- | duplicate a string, interspersing the character through the elements of the
1271: -- duplicated string
1272: c_intersperse :: Ptr Word8 -> Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> Word8 -> IO ()
1273: c_intersperse p1 p2 sz e = Pure.intersperse p1 p2 (checkedCast sz) e
1274: 
1275: -- | Quick sort bytes
1276: c_sort :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO ()
1277: c_sort ptr sz = Pure.quickSort ptr (checkedCast sz)
1278: 
1279: c_elem_index :: ByteArray# -> Word8 -> CSize -> IO CPtrdiff
1280: c_elem_index ba e sz = checkedCast <$!> Pure.elemIndex ba e (checkedCast sz)
1281: 
1282: cIsValidUtf8BA :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1283: cIsValidUtf8BA ba sz = bool_to_cint <$> Pure.isValidUtf8BA ba (checkedCast sz)
1284: 
1285: cIsValidUtf8 :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1286: cIsValidUtf8 ptr sz = bool_to_cint <$> Pure.isValidUtf8 ptr (checkedCast sz)
1287: 
1288: -- Pure module is compiled with `-fno-omit-yields` so it's always safe (it won't
1289: -- block on large inputs)
1290: 
1291: cIsValidUtf8BASafe :: ByteArray# -> CSize -> IO CInt
1292: cIsValidUtf8BASafe = cIsValidUtf8BA
1293: 
1294: cIsValidUtf8Safe :: Ptr Word8 -> CSize -> IO CInt
1295: cIsValidUtf8Safe = cIsValidUtf8
1296: 
1297: bool_to_cint :: Bool -> CInt
1298: bool_to_cint True = 1
1299: bool_to_cint False = 0
1300: 
1301: checkedCast :: (Bits a, Bits b, Integral a, Integral b) => a -> b
1302: checkedCast x =
1303:   fromMaybe (errorWithoutStackTrace "checkedCast: overflow")
1304:             (toIntegralSized x)
1305: 
1306: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1307: -- Haskell version of functions in itoa.c
1308: ----------------------------------------------------------------
1309: 
1310: c_int_dec :: CInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1311: c_int_dec = Pure.encodeSignedDec
1312: 
1313: c_long_long_int_dec :: CLLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1314: c_long_long_int_dec = Pure.encodeSignedDec
1315: 
1316: c_uint_dec :: CUInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1317: c_uint_dec = Pure.encodeUnsignedDec
1318: 
1319: c_long_long_uint_dec :: CULLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1320: c_long_long_uint_dec = Pure.encodeUnsignedDec
1321: 
1322: c_uint_hex :: CUInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1323: c_uint_hex = Pure.encodeUnsignedHex
1324: 
1325: c_long_long_uint_hex :: CULLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO (Ptr Word8)
1326: c_long_long_uint_hex = Pure.encodeUnsignedHex
1327: 
1328: c_int_dec_padded9 :: CInt -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1329: c_int_dec_padded9 = Pure.encodeUnsignedDecPadded 9
1330: 
1331: c_long_long_int_dec_padded18 :: CLLong -> Ptr Word8 -> IO ()
1332: c_long_long_int_dec_padded18 = Pure.encodeUnsignedDecPadded 18
1333: 
1334: #endif
